  ‚Ēā                ‚Ēā  (off,len)  ‚Ēā   in column    ‚Ēā                       ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā provenance     ‚Ēā none        ‚Ēā implicit       ‚Ēā explicit (owning      ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā                ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā                ‚Ēā row's gen-handle)     ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā owner          ‚Ēā silent UAF  ‚Ēā silent UAF     ‚Ēā caught (gen mismatch) ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā delete+reuse   ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā                ‚Ēā                       ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā relocatable /  ‚Ēā base lost   ‚Ēā no             ‚Ēā yes                   ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā serializable   ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā                ‚Ēā                       ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā cross-row      ‚Ēā none        ‚Ēā same-row only  ‚Ēā safe                  ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā safety         ‚Ēā             ‚Ēā                ‚Ēā                       ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  The unanimous DOD verdict: C is canonical ‚ÄĒ "a relative slice whose base is a
  generational handle," re-resolved through the same gen-check arche already
  does on every row deref. B is the named anti-pattern (Unity/flecs/Bevy all
  warn: a cached pointer is a latent dangling pointer ‚ÄĒ store the id,
  re-resolve). And the punchline that ties it to our parser case:

  ‚Ėé C degenerates to A for free when producer and consumer touch the same row in
  ‚Ėé the same scope (co-lifetime). The handle is constant, nothing can have been
  ‚Ėé deleted, so codegen elides it ‚Üí bare (offset,len), zero cost. The handle 
  ‚Ėé only re-emerges when the view escapes the owner's scope (stored in a column,
  ‚Ėé returned, passed to a later system) ‚ÄĒ exactly where Swift's ~Escapable 
  ‚Ėé would force you to stop too.

  So both traditions land on the same rule: store handles, pass views; a bare 
  span is legal only as a compile-time-proven same-scope specialization, never 
  as a cross-system carrier. rustc's integer-Span-into-immortal-SourceMap and
  Cyclone's region story are the two still out ‚ÄĒ I expect them to confirm the
  "immortal buffer ‚áí the offset is safe because the base never dies" angle,
  which is the other way C collapses to A (immortal region instead of
  same-scope). Holding synthesis for those two.

‚úĽ Saut√©ed for 15s

‚óŹ Agent "Research Rust slices/arenas/rustc spans" finished ¬∑ 5m 2s

‚óŹ Third thread back (Rust / rustc) ‚ÄĒ and it nails the precedent I most wanted:
  rustc stores integer spans, not &str. Every AST node carries Span{lo, hi: 
  BytePos(u32)} ‚ÄĒ absolute byte offsets into an immortal, append-only SourceMap
  ‚ÄĒ and never a borrowed slice. The documented rationale is exactly our
  concerns: lifetime infection (a &'a str in one node parameterizes the entire
  AST by the buffer's lifetime), compactness (8 bytes, interned when they
  spill), serialization / separate compilation (offsets persist to the
  incremental cache and rlibs; fat pointers can't), and decoupling from any
  transient parse buffer.

  It also adds the precise reason B is unsafe even within a struct: a stored fat
  pointer next to its owner is the self-referential-struct hazard ‚ÄĒ moves are
  memcpy and the pointer isn't fixed up, so it dangles the instant the row
  relocates. That's a fourth independent voice for "don't store the raw
  pointer."

  But here's the sharp nuance it surfaces ‚ÄĒ rustc's bare (offset,len) is safe 
  because the SourceMap is immortal and never freed. That gives the second way C
  collapses to A, distinct from the ECS one:

  - Same-scope co-lifetime (ECS brief) ‚Üí handle is constant, elided.
  - Immortal buffer (rustc) ‚Üí the base can never die, so the offset can't
  dangle; no handle needed.
  - Per-row-freeable buffer + view outlives it ‚Üí the only case that genuinely
  needs (handle, gen, offset, len) + the runtime gen-check.

  So the design rule is crystallizing: the handle is needed exactly when the 
  buffer can be freed independently of the view; otherwise the view degenerates 
  to a bare offset for free. Cyclone/regions is the last one out ‚ÄĒ it'll tell us
  whether the region/lifetime type-level machinery is worth importing to make
  "is the buffer immortal-or-co-lifetime?" a compile-time discharge rather than
  always paying the runtime check. Once it's in, I'll write the synthesis and
  the plan.

‚úĽ Baked for 22s

‚ĚĮ so we need a handle backed view? or just a handle to the row of data? then    
  where does the offset/len come from?                                          

‚óŹ Sharp question ‚ÄĒ and it cuts to the actual decision. Three things, in order:

  1. A handle to the row alone is not enough for a substring. A row handle
  addresses the whole buffer (raw). It tells you which bytes exist, not which 
  slice of them is "the method." You still need offset + len to pick the
  sub-range. So "just a handle" under-specifies ‚ÄĒ it gets you to the buffer, not
  to the substring.

  2. The offset/len come from the parse. Whoever scanned raw and found where
  "GET" starts and ends computed (offset, len). That's the only place the
  boundaries exist. The question was never "where do they come from" ‚ÄĒ it's
  where do they get stored, and that's the whole design choice.

  3. There are two safe placements, and which one you need depends on one thing:
  does the substring reference live in the same row as its buffer, or a 
  different one?

  - Same row ‚Üí no handle, no view type. Just sibling columns. Put
  method_off/method_len as int columns in the request row, next to raw. Anything
  iterating that row (an each/query) reads raw and the offsets together and
  slices on the spot. This is "bare spans" ‚ÄĒ but safe, because the offsets and
  the buffer are co-located and co-lifetime: delete the row, both vanish
  together; the offsets can never point at a buffer that's gone, because they
  die with it. The "provenance" the bare-span danger was missing is supplied
  implicitly by co-location ‚ÄĒ "this row." This is the common case: parse writes
  the offsets, the consumer each-es the same Request pool. No handle needed at 
  all.
  - Cross-row ‚Üí handle-backed view (handle, offset, len). Only if the reference
  must live in a different row than its buffer ‚ÄĒ e.g. parse routes a Routed row
  that needs to point back at the method-substring in a Request row. Now there's
  no implicit "this row" to lean on, so you store the gen-checked handle
  (locates + validates the buffer row) plus offset/len (select the sub-range).
  The handle is precisely the explicit replacement for the co-location
  provenance you lost by crossing rows.

  So: the handle-backed view exists only to recover, across rows, the safety 
  that co-location gives you for free within a row. The offset/len are the same
  in both cases (they come from the parse); the handle is the extra you pay
  exactly when the view escapes its buffer's row.

  Which means the real question for the HTTP flow is narrow: does method/target 
  need to outlive / escape the request row, or does the consumer read the same 
  row? If routing is an each over the Request pool (the producer/consumer shape
  in patterns.md), the substrings never escape ‚ÄĒ sibling offset/len columns, no 
  handle, no new type. You'd only reach for the handle-backed view if a
  substring reference had to be stored in a pool other than the one holding raw.
  My read is the request flow is the former ‚ÄĒ so the answer is "neither a
  handle nor a view type; co-located offset/len columns" ‚ÄĒ but tell me if you
  intend method to land in a separate pool from raw, because that's the one case
  that flips it.

‚úĽ Baked for 1m 0s

‚óŹ Agent "Research Cyclone and regions" finished ¬∑ 6m 34s
‚óŹ All four threads are in, and they converge ‚ÄĒ independently, from four
  different traditions ‚ÄĒ on a single model. Here's the synthesis.

  The convergence

  The cleanest framing is Cyclone's: a "view" has three orthogonal safety axes,
  and the whole "span vs slice vs handle-view" debate is just which axes you're 
  forced to pay for.

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź
  ‚Ēā   Axis   ‚Ēā              Question              ‚Ēā        Mechanism        ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā Temporal ‚Ēā does the backing storage still     ‚Ēā region / lifetime       ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā          ‚Ēā exist?                             ‚Ēā                         ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā Identity ‚Ēā is it still the same logical row?  ‚Ēā generational handle     ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā Spatial  ‚Ēā is the range in bounds?            ‚Ēā fat-pointer bounds      ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā          ‚Ēā                                    ‚Ēā check                   ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  And the rule ‚ÄĒ with who proves each part ‚ÄĒ is unanimous across all four:

  - Temporal is FREE for an immortal pool. A pool that lives the whole program
  is Cyclone's heap region `H ("never deallocated"), so the lifetime apparatus ‚ÄĒ
  region polymorphism, effects, capabilities, annotations ‚ÄĒ collapses to a 
  no-op**. This is also literally why **rustc stores (lo,hi) byte offsets into 
  an immortal SourceMap instead of &str: the buffer can't die, so the offset
  can't dangle. arche's static fixed-capacity pools satisfy this by
  construction.
  - Temporal is also free when the view and its buffer are co-lifetime ‚ÄĒ same
  row, same scope. They're created and destroyed together, so the offset can
  never outlive what it indexes.
  - You pay the Identity axis (a handle + one generation-compare) in exactly one
  case: the view escapes its buffer's row, and that row can be independently 
  deleted and its slot reused. That's the per-row use-after-free that regions 
  structurally cannot see (TT/Cyclone only free whole regions) ‚ÄĒ and the
  generational check is the cheap runtime patch. It is the same primitive as
  Vale's generational references, as arche's existing row handles, and as
  Cyclone's dynamic-region open check ‚ÄĒ just applied at row granularity.
  - Never store a raw (ptr,len) that can outlive its row. Rejected by all four:
  Rust's self-referential-struct ban (move = memcpy, the pointer isn't fixed
  up), the ECS "cached pointer = latent dangling pointer" rule
  (Unity/flecs/Bevy), C++'s string_view dangling footgun, and Cyclone's scoping
  rule. It bakes in an address arche is explicitly allowed to invalidate.

  What this does to our original question

  It reverses my "slices, not spans" instinct ‚ÄĒ and vindicates the code you
  already had.

  parse_request_line writing co-located offset/len columns in the same row as 
  raw is the co-lifetime case. It is safe by construction, and it is exactly the
  representation rustc chose (integer spans into a stable buffer) ‚ÄĒ for the
  same reasons: no lifetime infection, compact, serializable across separate
  compilation, decoupled from any transient buffer. The span wasn't the bug. A 
  stored raw slice would have been. So:

  - Same-row substring (the parse ‚Üí consume case): bare co-located offset/len 
  columns. No handle, no view type, zero runtime cost. The only obligation is
  that the consumer reads raw + offsets from the same row ‚ÄĒ which the
  producer/consumer each-over-one-pool shape already guarantees.
  - Handle-backed view (owner_handle, offset, len): the general form, needed 
  only when a substring reference must live in a different pool than raw. Real,
  but YAGNI until such a case actually appears ‚ÄĒ and when it does, it's a thin
  composition of mechanisms arche already has (handle + gen-check + bounds).
  - Stored raw fat pointer: a hard error, structurally. This is the one thing
  worth enforcing, matching your hard-errors-over-lints stance.

  Let me confirm scope before I finalize the plan ‚ÄĒ the research says don't
  build the handle-view yet, but there's a real fork on how much to
  enforce/capture now:

     maybe allow slices but only storable if the source is on the same row?

  Read 2 files (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Here are concrete examples, grounded in the actual HTTP parser you have. The
  current parse_request_line already writes spans ‚ÄĒ method_start, method_len,
  target_start, target_len (4 int columns) ‚ÄĒ into each Request row. The research
  says that's correct but verbose; the same-row rule lets you replace it with
  slice columns.

  A. Same-row slice columns ‚ÄĒ ALLOWED (this is your parser, rewritten)

  Request :: arche {
    raw    :: [512]char,   // received bytes ‚ÄĒ the row OWNS this buffer
    method :: []char,      // VIEW column: a slice into THIS row's raw
    target :: []char,      // VIEW column: another slice into raw
    ok     :: int,
  }
  [16]Request;

  parse_request_line :: each (query { raw, method, target, ok }) {
    ok = 0;
    n := str.strlen(raw);
    if (n >= 5) {
      sp1 := str.find_char(raw, 0, n, ' ');
      sp2 := str.find_char(raw, sp1 + 1, n, ' ');
      if (sp1 < n && sp2 < n) {
        method = raw[0 : sp1];          // slice of THIS row's raw ‚Üí same-row ‚Üí
  STORABLE ‚úď
        tstart := sp1 + 1;
        tend   := sp2; q := str.find_char(raw, tstart, sp2, '?');
        if (q < sp2) { tend = q; }       // trim ?query
        target = raw[tstart : tend];     // ditto ‚úď
        ok = 1;
      }
    }
  }

  route :: each (query { method, target, ok }) {        // consumer just USES
  the views
    if (ok == 1) { fmt.printf("%s %s\n", method, target); }
  }

  The 4 int columns + manual raw[method_start : method_start+method_len]
  re-slicing in every consumer collapse to method. Safe because method's backing
  (raw) is in the same row ‚ÄĒ delete the row and raw, method, target vanish
  together; the view can't outlive what it points at.

  B. Cross-row store ‚ÄĒ HARD ERROR (and why the rule exists)

  Request :: arche { raw :: [512]char, method :: []char }
  Audit   :: arche { verb :: []char }      // a SEPARATE pool ‚ÄĒ independent
  lifetime
  [16]Request; [64]Audit;

  log_verb :: each (query { raw, method } as r) {
    method = raw[0:3];
    insert(Audit { verb: method })(_:, _:);  // ‚úó storing a slice of Request.raw
  into Audit ‚Ä¶
    delete(r)(_:);                           //   then freeing the Request row ‚Üí
  Audit.verb dangles (UAF)
  }

  The rule catches it: verb's source (Request.raw) is not in the same row as
  verb (it lives in Audit, a different pool with its own lifetime). Rejected at
  compile time ‚ÄĒ exactly the case bare spans would let through silently.

  C. The two escapes when a substring genuinely must cross pools

  // C1 ‚ÄĒ copy: Audit owns its bytes, borrows nothing
  Audit :: arche { verb :: [8]char }
  insert(Audit { verb: copy raw[0:3] })(_:, _:);   // 3 bytes copied into
  Audit's own storage ‚Üí safe

  // C2 ‚ÄĒ handle-backed view: no copy, carries provenance + gen-check (YAGNI /
  illustrative syntax)
  Audit :: arche { src :: handle(Request), off :: int, len :: int }
  insert(Audit { src: r, off: 0, len: 3 })(_:, _:);          // store the HANDLE
  + span, not a raw slice
  // consumer: raw := Request[src].raw;  (gen-checked ‚ÄĒ traps if that row was
  deleted)
  //           verb := raw[off : off+len];

  The punchline you're looking for: your HTTP server has no cross-row case.
  Parse writes into the Request row it's iterating; respond reads from the
  connection row it's iterating ‚ÄĒ everything is same-row (Example A). B and C
  simply never arise in the server. The cross-row case only shows up in
  something like a cache or index that holds substrings of other pools' buffers 
  across time ‚ÄĒ and that's precisely where you'd want C2's handle so a stale
  entry traps instead of corrupting. Which is why the verdict is: ship A + the
  hard error now, leave C2 unbuilt until a real cross-row need appears.

     ‚ē≠‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ēģ
     ‚Ēā Proc elimination via ECS decomposition ‚ÄĒ no routine, funcs stay pure    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Context                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā proc is being removed from the language except #foreign externs and     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā primitives (@syscall/@intrinsic).                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā A four-lens analysis (data-oriented, PL-theory, ergonomics, minimalist) ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā converged on adding a routine                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā kind (a bounded free monad ‚Č° compile-time-spliced callable) plus        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pool-reads-inside-funcs. The user                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā rejected both, and correctly:                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - A func that reads a mutable pool is not pure ‚ÄĒ that read belongs in a ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā system, not a func. Funcs                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā stay strictly pure (params + :: constants only). func_impure stays      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā strict.                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - There must be no intra-row monadic residue and no routine. ECS        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā already replaces value-level                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā bind: system 1 produces n (writes a column); system 2 consumes n (reads ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā it) and does the n+1                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā step. The schedule orders writer-before-reader within one pass          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (seq/data-derived), so a                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā result-dependent step is just a producer‚Üíconsumer data edge, not a      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā callee. Branch-on-result ‚Üí the                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā producer routes rows into type-specific pools; unbounded loop ‚Üí         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā bulk-read + columnar scan (+ a                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pushback column for over-read), not per-byte sequencing.                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā So the model is pure ECS: proc ‚Üí #foreign/primitives only; every        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā effectful or pool-touching op ‚Üí a                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā system over request/result pools, ordered by data edges; funcs stay     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pure; no new kind. It needs almost no                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā new language surface ‚ÄĒ it is a rewrite onto mechanisms that already     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā exist (each/system/map/query/                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā insert/delete/#run/@drop), plus the lint flips. Accepted costs: no      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā called effectful/stateful helpers                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (more setup per op), and a genuinely unbounded no-read-ahead            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā interactive loop costs a schedule tick per                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā round-trip. Rollout: mechanisms first, one module at a time, build      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā green throughout, flip lints only once                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā stdlib is clean.                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Already landed & green (keep): fmt.fail (pure func builds the abort     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Eff; the condition is system                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā control flow ‚ÄĒ the assert replacement), and the char-column query-read  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā codegen fix (systems can now read                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā [N]char columns ‚ÄĒ needed for buffer/line scanning).                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Views & substrings: the same-row slice rule (resolved by four-tradition ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā research)                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Cross-tradition research (Cyclone/regions, Rust+rustc spans, ECS        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā handles, Swift ~Escapable/Vale)                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā converged on one model for "pass a borrowed substring of a buffer       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā between systems without UAF":                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - A view has three orthogonal axes ‚ÄĒ temporal (does storage exist),     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā identity (same logical row),                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā spatial (in bounds). For arche's immortal, non-relocating pools the     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā temporal axis is a no-op                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (Cyclone heap-region `H; rustc stores integer BytePos spans into the    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā immortal SourceMap for                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā exactly this reason). Identity is the only axis pure regions miss ‚ÄĒ     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā it's the per-row free/reuse                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā case, covered by arche's existing generational handle (== Vale          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā generational reference).                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Rule: a slice ([]char/[]byte) column is storable iff its source       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā buffer is in the same row.                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Same-row ‚áí co-lifetime ‚áí can't dangle (the substring and its buffer die ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā together). This is the parse                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā case and it is all the HTTP server ever needs.                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Storing a slice whose source is a different row/pool is a HARD ERROR  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (independent lifetimes ‚Üí                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā UAF). Decision: hard-error only, defer the escapes. Cross-row simply    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā won't compile; the manual fix                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā is "copy the bytes into an owned buffer column" (no first-class         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā blessing built yet). The                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā handle-backed view (handle, off, len) gen-checked on materialization is ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the eventual cross-row                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā mechanism but is YAGNI ‚ÄĒ no current program needs it; it only arises    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā for a cache/index holding                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā substrings across pools over time. Build it when a real case appears,   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā not before.                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - A bare span (off,len) int pair is vindicated for the same-row case    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (it's what rustc ships) but a                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā slice column is the more ergonomic same-row form (consumer says method, ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā not raw[ms:ms+ml]).                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Concrete change: rewrite stdlib/http/http.arche parse_request_line from ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the 4 span columns                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (method_start/len, target_start/len) to same-row slice columns method   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā :: []char, target :: []char                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (method = raw[0:sp1]). Add the same-row-source check as a hard error in ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā semantic analysis (a slice                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā stored into a column must trace to a column of the same archetype).     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Capture the model in docs/design/                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (views, substrings, the same-row rule, the three axes). Defer the       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā handle-view.                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Mechanisms (build/confirm first)                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 1. Lints (the discipline). Strengthen the proc rule (semantic.c         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā lint_proc_decl ~4564): a proc is                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā legal only if #foreign/@syscall/@intrinsic; every other proc is an      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā error naming the fix (‚Üí a                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā func/system/each/map, or decompose across systems). Promote it +        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā func_impure (W0003, keeps funcs                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā pure ‚ÄĒ do not relax for pool reads) + pool_index_outside_query (W0029)  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā to error-by-default via                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā g_werror in ensure_init (sem_diagnostics.c ~211). Promote after stdlib  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā is converted (flipping                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā first bricks every program that imports stdlib).                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 2. Data-edge ordering. Bounded dependent stages order with explicit     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā seq({ producer, consumer }) today                                       ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā 3. @drop close-on-delete already exists (the column-type-targeted       ‚Ēā
